stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">\xc9\x99-<span style="font-size:90%">ZORZ</span></i></a>, <small>also</small> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">e\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">AY</span>-zorz</i></a>;<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">A\xc3\xa7ores</i> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[\xc9\x90\xcb\x88so\xc9\xbe\xc9\xa8\xca\x83]</a></span>), officially the <b>Autonomous Region of the Azores</b> (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">Regi\xc3\xa3o Aut\xc3\xb3noma dos A\xc3\xa7ores</i>), is one of the two <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Regions_of_Portugal" title="Autonomous Regions of Portugal">autonomous regions of Portugal</a> (along with <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>). It is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> composed of nine <a href="/wiki/High_island" title="High island">volcanic islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesia</a> region of the North Atlantic Ocean, about 1,400&#160;km (870&#160;mi) west of <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, about 1,500&#160;km (930&#160;mi) northwest of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, and about 1,930&#160;km (1,200&#160;mi) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.\n</p><p>Its main industries are agriculture, <a href="/wiki/Dairy_farming" title="Dairy farming">dairy farming</a>, livestock, <a href="/wiki/Fishing_in_Portugal" title="Fishing in Portugal">fishing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Portugal" title="Tourism in Portugal">tourism</a>, which is becoming the major service activity in the region. The government of the Azores employs a large percentage of the population directly or indirectly in the service and tertiary sectors. The main city of the Azores is <a href="/wiki/Ponta_Delgada" title="Ponta Delgada">Ponta Delgada</a>. The culture, dialect, cuisine, and traditions of the Azorean islands vary considerably, because these remote islands were settled sporadically over a span of two centuries.\n</p><p>There are nine major Azorean islands and an islet cluster, in three main groups. These are <a href="/wiki/Flores_Island_(Azores)" title="Flores Island (Azores)">Flores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corvo_Island" title="Corvo Island">Corvo</a>, to the west; <a href="/wiki/Graciosa" title="Graciosa">Graciosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terceira_Island" title="Terceira Island">Terceira</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jorge_Island" title="S\xc3\xa3o Jorge Island">S\xc3\xa3o Jorge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pico_Island" title="Pico Island">Pico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Faial_Island" title="Faial Island">Faial</a> in the centre; and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island" title="S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island">S\xc3\xa3o Miguel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_Island" title="Santa Maria Island">Santa Maria</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Formigas" title="Formigas">Formigas Reef</a> to the east. They extend for more than 600&#160;km (370&#160;mi) and lie in a northwest\xe2\x80\x93southeast direction. All of the islands have volcanic origins, although some, such as Santa Maria, have had no recorded activity in the time since the islands were settled several centuries ago. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pico" title="Mount Pico">Mount Pico</a>, on the island of Pico, is the highest point in Portugal, at 2,351&#160;m (7,713&#160;ft). If measured from their base at the bottom of the ocean to their peaks, which thrust high above the surface of the Atlantic, the Azores are among the tallest mountains on the planet.\n</p><p>The climate of the Azores is very mild for such a northerly location, being influenced by its distance from the continents and by the passing <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>. Because of the marine influence, temperatures remain mild year-round. Daytime temperatures normally fluctuate between 16&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and 25&#160;\xc2\xb0C (77&#160;\xc2\xb0F) depending on season.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Temperatures above 30&#160;\xc2\xb0C (86&#160;\xc2\xb0F) or below 3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (37&#160;\xc2\xb0F) are unknown in the major population centres. It is also generally wet and cloudy.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Discovery_and_settlement"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Discovery and settlement</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Iberian_Union"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Iberian Union</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Liberal_Wars"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Liberal Wars</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Modern_period"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext">Modern period</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Physical_geography"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Physical geography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Geology"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Geology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Biome"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Biome</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11"><a href="#Hurricanes"><span class="tocnumber">2.4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Hurricanes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Population"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Population</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Emigration"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Emigration</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Politics"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Aviation"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Aviation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Marine_transportation"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Marine transportation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Azores" title="History of the Azores">History of the Azores</a></div>\n<p>A small number of alleged <a href="/wiki/Hypogeum" title="Hypogeum">hypogea</a> (underground structures carved into rocks) have been identified on the islands of Corvo, Santa Maria, and Terceira by Portuguese archaeologist Nuno Ribeiro, who speculated that they might date back 2,000 years, implying a human presence on the island before the Portuguese.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> These kinds of structures have been used in the Azores to store grain. Any suggestions by Ribeiro that they might be burial sites are unconfirmed. Detailed examination and dating to authenticate the validity of these speculations is lacking; thus it is unclear whether these structures are natural or human-made and whether they predate the 15th-century Portuguese colonization of the Azores.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_and_settlement">Discovery and settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Discovery and settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg/170px-Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg/255px-Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg/340px-Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="783" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Under the direction of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Henry_the_Navigator" title="Prince Henry the Navigator">Prince Henry the Navigator</a>, the Azores were discovered and populated in the early 1400s.</div></div></div>\n<p>The islands were known to Europeans in the 14th century, and parts of them appear in the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Atlas" title="Catalan Atlas">Catalan Atlas</a>. In 1427, a captain sailing for <a href="/wiki/Prince_Henry_the_Navigator" title="Prince Henry the Navigator">Prince Henry the Navigator</a>, possibly <a href="/wiki/Gon%C3%A7alo_Velho_Cabral" title="Gon\xc3\xa7alo Velho Cabral">Gon\xc3\xa7alo Velho</a>, may have rediscovered the Azores, but this is not certain. In <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Ashe_(writer)" title="Thomas Ashe (writer)">Thomas Ashe</a>\'s 1813 work, <i>A History of the Azores</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-History1813_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History1813-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> the author identified a <a href="/wiki/Flemish_people" title="Flemish people">Fleming</a>, Joshua Vander Berg of <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a>, who made landfall in the archipelago during a storm on his way to Lisbon.<sup id="cite_ref-History1813_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History1813-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He stated that the Portuguese explored the area and claimed it for Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-History1813_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History1813-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Other stories note the discovery of the first islands (S\xc3\xa3o Miguel, Santa Maria and Terceira) by sailors in the service of Henry the Navigator, although there are few documents to support the claims.\n</p><p>Although it is commonly said that the archipelago received its name from <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">a\xc3\xa7or</i> (<a href="/wiki/Northern_goshawk" title="Northern goshawk">goshawk</a> in Portuguese), a common bird at the time of discovery, it is unlikely that the bird nested or hunted on the islands.\n</p><p>There were no large animals on Santa Maria, so after its discovery and before settlement began, sheep were let loose on the island to supply future settlers with food. Settlement did not take place right away, however. Gon\xc3\xa7alo Velho Cabral gathered resources and settlers for the next three years (1433\xe2\x80\x931436) and sailed to establish colonies, first on Santa Maria and then on S\xc3\xa3o Miguel. Settlers cleared bush and rocks to plant crops: grain, grapevines, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>, and other plants suitable for local use and of commercial value. They brought domesticated animals, such as chickens, rabbits, cattle, sheep, goats, and pigs, and built houses and established villages.\n</p><p>The archipelago was largely settled from mainland Portugal. S\xc3\xa3o Miguel was first settled in 1449, the settlers \xe2\x80\x93 mainly from the <a href="/wiki/Estremadura_Province_(historical)" title="Estremadura Province (historical)">Estremadura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alto_Alentejo_Province" title="Alto Alentejo Province">Alto Alentejo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> areas of mainland Portugal, under the command of Gon\xc3\xa7alo Velho Cabral \xe2\x80\x93 landed at the site of modern-day <a href="/wiki/Povoa%C3%A7%C3%A3o,_Azores" title="Povoa\xc3\xa7\xc3\xa3o, Azores">Povoa\xc3\xa7\xc3\xa3o</a>. Many of the early settlers were Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi Jews</a> who were banished/exiled there by the inquisition on mainland Portugal - many had well known Sephardi surnames such as: Pereira, Oliveira, Cardoso, Pimentel, Pinto, Rodrigues, Mendes, or Nunes. \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azores_old_map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Azores_old_map.jpg/220px-Azores_old_map.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Azores_old_map.jpg/330px-Azores_old_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Azores_old_map.jpg/440px-Azores_old_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2104" data-file-height="1480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azores_old_map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1584 map of the Azores Islands</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1522, <a href="/wiki/Vila_Franca_do_Campo" title="Vila Franca do Campo">Vila Franca do Campo</a>, then the capital of the island, was devastated by an <a href="/wiki/1522_Vila_Franca_earthquake" title="1522 Vila Franca earthquake">earthquake and landslide</a> that killed about 5,000 people, and the capital was moved to <a href="/wiki/Ponta_Delgada" title="Ponta Delgada">Ponta Delgada</a>. The town of Vila Franca do Campo was rebuilt on the original site and today is a thriving fishing and yachting port. Ponta Delgada received its city status in 1546. From the first settlement, the pioneers applied themselves to agriculture, and by the 15th century Graciosa exported wheat, barley, wine and brandy. The goods were sent to Terceira largely because of the proximity of the island.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ribeira_Grande,_S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island,_Azores_-_panoramio_(7)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ribeira_Grande%2C_S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island%2C_Azores_-_panoramio_%287%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Ribeira_Grande%2C_S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island%2C_Azores_-_panoramio_%287%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ribeira_Grande%2C_S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island%2C_Azores_-_panoramio_%287%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Ribeira_Grande%2C_S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island%2C_Azores_-_panoramio_%287%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ribeira_Grande%2C_S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island%2C_Azores_-_panoramio_%287%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Ribeira_Grande%2C_S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island%2C_Azores_-_panoramio_%287%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="431" data-file-height="665" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ribeira_Grande,_S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island,_Azores_-_panoramio_(7)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Frutuoso" title="Gaspar Frutuoso">Gaspar Frutuoso</a> wrote <i><a href="/wiki/Saudades_da_Terra" title="Saudades da Terra">Saudades da Terra</a></i>, the first history of the Azores and <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesia</a>, in the 1580s.</div></div></div>\n<p>The first reference to the island of S\xc3\xa3o Jorge was made in 1439, but the actual date of discovery is unknown. In 1443, the island was already inhabited, but active settlement only began with the arrival of the noble Flemish native <a href="/wiki/Willem_van_der_Haegen" title="Willem van der Haegen">Willem van der Haegen</a>. Arriving at <a href="/wiki/Topo_(Calheta)" title="Topo (Calheta)">Topo</a>, where he lived and died, he became known as <i>Guilherme da Silveira</i> to the islanders. <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Vaz_Corte-Real" title="Jo\xc3\xa3o Vaz Corte-Real">Jo\xc3\xa3o Vaz Corte-Real</a> received the captaincy of the island in 1483. <a href="/wiki/Velas,_Azores" title="Velas, Azores">Velas</a> became a town before the end of the 15th century. By 1490, there were 2,000 Flemings living in the islands of Terceira, Pico, Faial, S\xc3\xa3o Jorge and Flores. Because there was such a large Flemish settlement, the Azores became known as the Flemish Islands or the Isles of Flanders. Prince Henry the Navigator was responsible for this settlement. His sister, <a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Portugal,_Duchess_of_Burgundy" title="Isabella of Portugal, Duchess of Burgundy">Isabel</a>, was married to <a href="/wiki/Philip_the_Good" title="Philip the Good">Duke Philip of Burgundy</a>, of which Flanders was a part. There was a revolt against Philip\'s rule, and disease and hunger became rampant. Isabel appealed to Henry to allow some of the unruly Flemings to settle in the Azores. He granted this and supplied them with the necessary transportation and goods.\n</p><p>The settlement of the unoccupied islands started in 1439 with people mainly from the continental provinces of Algarve and <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a>. In 1583, <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a>, as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Portuguese_monarchs" title="List of Portuguese monarchs">king of Portugal</a>, sent his fleet to clear the Azores of a combined multinational force of adventurers, mercenaries, volunteers and soldiers who were attempting to establish the Azores as a staging post for a rival <a href="/wiki/Pretender" title="Pretender">pretender</a> to the Portuguese throne. Following the success of his fleet at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ponta_Delgada" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Ponta Delgada">Battle of Ponta Delgada</a> captured enemies were hanged from yardarms, as they were considered pirates by Philip II. Opponents receiving the news variously portrayed Philip II as a despot or "<a href="/wiki/Black_legend_(Spain)" title="Black legend (Spain)">Black Legend</a>"; the sort of insult widely made against contemporary monarchs engaged in aggressive empire building and the <a href="/wiki/European_wars_of_religion" title="European wars of religion">European wars of religion</a>. An English <a href="/wiki/Azores_Voyage_of_1589" title="Azores Voyage of 1589">raid of the Azores</a> in 1589 successfully plundered some harbouring ships and islands; a repeat eight years later, the <a href="/wiki/Islands_Voyage" title="Islands Voyage">Islands Voyage</a>, failed. Spain held the Azores under the "Babylonian captivity" of 1580\xe2\x80\x931642. In the late 16th century, the Azores and Madeira began to face problems of overpopulation. Spawning from that particular economic problem, some of the people began to emigrate to Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-ImperialAge1989_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ImperialAge1989-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iberian_Union">Iberian Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Iberian Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Desembarcoislasterceiras.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Desembarcoislasterceiras.jpg/220px-Desembarcoislasterceiras.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Desembarcoislasterceiras.jpg/330px-Desembarcoislasterceiras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Desembarcoislasterceiras.jpg/440px-Desembarcoislasterceiras.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="622" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Desembarcoislasterceiras.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Azores" title="Conquest of the Azores">Battle of Terceira</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Portuguese_Succession" title="War of the Portuguese Succession">War of the Portuguese Succession</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Azores" title="Conquest of the Azores">Conquest of the Azores</a></div>\n<p>Following the death of <a href="/wiki/Henry,_King_of_Portugal" title="Henry, King of Portugal">Henry, the Cardinal-King of Portugal</a> in 1580, the nation fell into a dynastic crisis with <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_succession_crisis_of_1580#Claimants_to_the_throne" title="Portuguese succession crisis of 1580">various pretenders</a> to the Crown of Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-MeloBento34_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MeloBento34-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Following his proclamation in Santar\xc3\xa9m, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio,_Prior_of_Crato" title="Ant\xc3\xb3nio, Prior of Crato">Ant\xc3\xb3nio, Prior of Crato</a> was acclaimed in the Azores in 1580 (through his envoy Ant\xc3\xb3nio da Costa) but was expelled from the continent following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alc%C3%A2ntara_(1580)" title="Battle of Alc\xc3\xa2ntara (1580)">Battle of Alc\xc3\xa2ntara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MeloBento34_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MeloBento34-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Yet, through the administration of Cipriano de Figueiredo, governor of Terceira (who continued to govern Terceira in the name of ill-fated, former King <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_of_Portugal" title="Sebastian of Portugal">Sebastian of Portugal</a>), the Azoreans resisted attempts to conquer the islands (including specifically at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Salga" title="Battle of Salga">Battle of Salga</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-MeloBento36_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MeloBento36-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It was Figueiredo and Violante do Canto who helped organize a resistance on Terceira that influenced some of the response of the other islands, even as internal politics and support for Philip\'s faction increased on the other islands (including specifically on S\xc3\xa3o Miguel, where the Gon\xc3\xa7alvez da C\xc3\xa2mara family supported the Spanish pretender).<sup id="cite_ref-MeloBento36_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MeloBento36-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Azores were the last part of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> to resist Philip\'s reign over Portugal (<a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> resisted any official recognition), until the defeat of forces loyal to the Prior of Crato with the <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Azores" title="Conquest of the Azores">Conquest of the Azores</a> in 1583. Portuguese control resumed with the end of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> in 1640, and the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a>, not by the professional military, who were occupied with warfare on the Portuguese mainland, but by local people attacking a fortified <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castilian</a> garrison.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberal_Wars">Liberal Wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Liberal Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DpedroI-brasil-full.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/DpedroI-brasil-full.jpg/170px-DpedroI-brasil-full.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/DpedroI-brasil-full.jpg/255px-DpedroI-brasil-full.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/DpedroI-brasil-full.jpg/340px-DpedroI-brasil-full.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1265" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DpedroI-brasil-full.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">King-Emperor Pedro IV &amp; I</a> planned and launched his campaign in the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Wars" title="Liberal Wars">Liberal Wars</a> from the Azores in name of his daughter <a href="/wiki/Maria_II_of_Portugal" title="Maria II of Portugal">Queen Maria II</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Wars" title="Liberal Wars">Portuguese Civil War</a> (1828\xe2\x80\x931834) had strong repercussions in the Azores. In 1829, in <a href="/wiki/Praia_da_Vit%C3%B3ria" title="Praia da Vit\xc3\xb3ria">Praia da Vit\xc3\xb3ria</a>, the liberals won over the <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">absolutists</a>, making Terceira Island the main headquarters of the new Portuguese regime and also where the Council of Regency (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">Conselho de Reg\xc3\xaancia</i>) of <a href="/wiki/Maria_II_of_Portugal" title="Maria II of Portugal">Maria II of Portugal</a> was established. Beginning in 1868, Portugal issued its stamps overprinted with "<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">A\xc3\x87ORES</i>" for use in the islands. Between 1892 and 1906, it also issued separate stamps for the three administrative districts of the time.\n</p><p>During the 18th and 19th centuries, Graciosa was host to many prominent figures, including <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-Ren%C3%A9_de_Chateaubriand" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois-Ren\xc3\xa9 de Chateaubriand">Chateaubriand</a>, the French writer who passed through upon his escape to America during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>; <a href="/wiki/Almeida_Garrett" title="Almeida Garrett">Almeida Garrett</a>, the Portuguese poet who visited an uncle and wrote some poetry while there; and <a href="/wiki/Albert_I,_Prince_of_Monaco" title="Albert I, Prince of Monaco">Prince Albert of Monaco</a>, the 19th-century oceanographer who led several expeditions in the waters of the Azores. He arrived on his yacht <i>Hirondelle</i>, and visited the <i>furna da caldeira</i>, the noted hot springs grotto. In 1869, the author <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain" title="Mark Twain">Mark Twain</a> published <i><a href="/wiki/The_Innocents_Abroad" title="The Innocents Abroad">The Innocents Abroad</a></i>, a travel book, where he described his time in the Azores.\n</p><p>From 1836 to 1976, the archipelago was divided into three districts, equivalent (except in area) to those in the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Portugal#Districts" title="Administrative divisions of Portugal">Portuguese mainland</a>. The division was arbitrary and did not follow the natural island groups, rather reflecting the location of each district capital on the three main cities (none of which were on the western group).\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo</b> consisted of Terceira, S\xc3\xa3o Jorge, and Graciosa, with the capital at <a href="/wiki/Angra_do_Hero%C3%ADsmo" title="Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo">Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo</a> on Terceira. <b>Horta</b> consisted of Pico, Faial, Flores, and Corvo, with the capital at <a href="/wiki/Horta,_Azores" title="Horta, Azores">Horta</a> on Faial. <b>Ponta Delgada</b> consisted of S\xc3\xa3o Miguel and Santa Maria, with the capital at <a href="/wiki/Ponta_Delgada" title="Ponta Delgada">Ponta Delgada</a> on S\xc3\xa3o Miguel.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_period">Modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:158px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crest_of_the_Azores.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Crest_of_the_Azores.gif" decoding="async" width="156" height="156" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="156" data-file-height="156" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crest_of_the_Azores.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Symbol of the Azorean autonomist movement in the 19th century</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1931, the Azores (together with Madeira and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a>) revolted against the <a href="/wiki/Ditadura_Nacional" title="Ditadura Nacional">Ditadura Nacional</a> and were held briefly by military rebels.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>\nIn 1943, during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the Portuguese ruler <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Oliveira_Salazar" title="Ant\xc3\xb3nio de Oliveira Salazar">Ant\xc3\xb3nio de Oliveira Salazar</a> leased air and naval bases in the Azores to Great Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The occupation of these facilities in October 1943 was codenamed <i><a href="/wiki/Operation_Alacrity" title="Operation Alacrity">Operation Alacrity</a></i> by the British.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> This was a key turning point in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a>, enabling the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">U.S. Army Air Forces</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">U.S. Navy</a> to provide aerial coverage in the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_gap" title="Mid-Atlantic gap">Mid-Atlantic gap</a>. This helped them to protect <a href="/wiki/Convoy" title="Convoy">convoys</a> and to hunt hostile German <a href="/wiki/U-boat" title="U-boat">U-boats</a>. In 1944, the U.S. constructed a small and short-lived air base on the island of Santa Maria. In 1945, a new base was constructed on the island of Terceira, named <a href="/wiki/Lajes_Field" title="Lajes Field">Lajes Field</a>. This air base is in an area called Lajes, a broad, flat sea terrace that had been a large farm. Lajes Field is a plateau rising out of the sea on the northeast corner of the island. This air base is a joint American and Portuguese venture. Lajes Field continues to support the American and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Armed_Forces" title="Portuguese Armed Forces">Portuguese Armed Forces</a>.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Azores_Liberation_Front.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Flag_of_the_Azores_Liberation_Front.jpg/220px-Flag_of_the_Azores_Liberation_Front.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Flag_of_the_Azores_Liberation_Front.jpg/330px-Flag_of_the_Azores_Liberation_Front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Flag_of_the_Azores_Liberation_Front.jpg/440px-Flag_of_the_Azores_Liberation_Front.jpg 2x" data-file-width="487" data-file-height="283" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Azores_Liberation_Front.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Azores_Liberation_Front" title="Azores Liberation Front">Azores Liberation Front</a>\'s flag preceded the modern <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Azores" title="Flag of the Azores">Azorean flag</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, U.S. Navy <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_P-3_Orion" title="Lockheed P-3 Orion">P-3 Orion</a> <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare" title="Anti-submarine warfare">anti-submarine warfare</a> squadrons patrolled the North Atlantic Ocean for <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Navy" title="Soviet Navy">Soviet Navy</a> submarines and surface warships. Since its opening, Lajes Field has been used for refuelling American <a href="/wiki/Cargo_aircraft" title="Cargo aircraft">cargo planes</a> bound for Europe, Africa, and the Middle East. The U.S. Navy keeps a small <a href="/wiki/Squadron_(naval)" title="Squadron (naval)">squadron</a> of its ships at the harbor of <a href="/wiki/Praia_da_Vit%C3%B3ria" title="Praia da Vit\xc3\xb3ria">Praia da Vit\xc3\xb3ria</a>, three kilometres (1.9 miles) southeast of Lajes Field. The airfield also has a small commercial terminal handling scheduled and chartered passenger flights from the other islands in the Azores, Europe, Africa, and North America.\n</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> of 1974, which deposed the <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a> dictatorship in Lisbon, Portugal and its territories across the world entered into a period of great political uncertainty. The <a href="/wiki/Azores_Liberation_Front" title="Azores Liberation Front">Azorean Liberation Front</a> attempted to take advantage of this instability immediately after the revolution, hoping to establish an independent Azores, until operations ceased in 1975. \n</p><p>In 1976, the Azores became the Autonomous Region of the Azores (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">Regi\xc3\xa3o Aut\xc3\xb3noma dos A\xc3\xa7ores</i>), one of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous regions of Portugal">autonomous regions of Portugal</a>, and the subdistricts of the Azores were eliminated. In 2003, the Azores saw international attention when United States President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>, Spanish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada Aznar">Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada Aznar</a> and Portuguese Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Manuel Barroso">Jos\xc3\xa9 Manuel Dur\xc3\xa3o Barroso</a> held a summit there days before the commencement of the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azores-map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Azores-map.png/260px-Azores-map.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Azores-map.png/390px-Azores-map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Azores-map.png/520px-Azores-map.png 2x" data-file-width="2960" data-file-height="1808" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azores-map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Azores</div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right;">\n\n<caption>Surface areas of the Azores Islands\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="width:130px;" rowspan="2">Island\n</th>\n<th colspan="2">Area\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="width:50px;">km<sup>2</sup>\n</th>\n<th style="width:50px;">sq mi\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island" title="S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island">S\xc3\xa3o Miguel</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">759\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">293\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Pico_Island" title="Pico Island">Pico</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">446\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">172\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Terceira_Island" title="Terceira Island">Terceira</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">403\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">156\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jorge_Island" title="S\xc3\xa3o Jorge Island">S\xc3\xa3o Jorge</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">246\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">95\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Faial_Island" title="Faial Island">Faial</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">173\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">67\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Flores_Island_(Azores)" title="Flores Island (Azores)">Flores</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">143\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">55\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_Island" title="Santa Maria Island">Santa Maria</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">97\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">37\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Graciosa_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Graciosa Island">Graciosa</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">62\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">24\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Corvo_Island" title="Corvo Island">Corvo</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">17\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">7\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The archipelago of the Azores is located in the middle of the northern hemisphere of the Atlantic Ocean and extends along a west-northwest to east-southeast orientation (between 36.5\xc2\xb0\xe2\x80\x9340\xc2\xb0 North <a href="/wiki/Latitudes" class="mw-redirect" title="Latitudes">latitudes</a> and 24.5\xc2\xb0\xe2\x80\x9331.5\xc2\xb0 West <a href="/wiki/Longitudes" class="mw-redirect" title="Longitudes">longitudes</a>) in an area approximately 600 kilometres (373 miles) wide. The islands of the Azores emerged from what is called the <a href="/wiki/Azores_Plateau" title="Azores Plateau">Azores Plateau</a>, a 5.8&#160;million km<sup>2</sup> region that is morphologically accented by a depth of 2,000 metres (6,600 feet).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Machado2008p14_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Machado2008p14-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The nine islands that compose the archipelago occupy a surface area of 2,346&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (906&#160;sq&#160;mi), that includes both the main islands and many islets located in their vicinities. They range in surface area from the largest, S\xc3\xa3o Miguel, at 759&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (293&#160;sq&#160;mi) to the smallest, Corvo, at approximately 17&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (7&#160;sq&#160;mi). Each of the islands has its own distinct geomorphological characteristics that make them unique: Corvo (the smallest island) is a crater of a major Plinian eruption; Flores (its neighbor on the North American Plate) is a rugged island carved by many valleys and escarpments; Faial is characterized for its <a href="/wiki/Volcano#Shield_volcanoes" title="Volcano">shield volcano</a> and caldera (<a href="/wiki/Cabe%C3%A7o_Gordo" title="Cabe\xc3\xa7o Gordo">Cabe\xc3\xa7o Gordo</a>); <a href="/wiki/Pico_Island" title="Pico Island">Pico</a>, is the highest point, at 2,351 meters (7,713&#160;ft), in the Azores and continental Portugal; Graciosa is known for its active Furnas do Enxofre and mixture of volcanic cones and plains; S\xc3\xa3o Jorge is a long slender island, formed from <a href="/wiki/Types_of_volcanic_eruptions" title="Types of volcanic eruptions">fissural eruptions</a> over thousands of years; Terceira, almost circular, is the location of one of the largest craters in the region; S\xc3\xa3o Miguel is the largest island and is pitted with many large craters and fields of spatter cones; and Santa Maria, the oldest island, is heavily eroded, being one of the few places to encounter brown sandy beaches in the archipelago.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Sete_Cidades_(panorama).JPG" class="image" title="The Lagoa das Sete Cidades, located within the Sete Cidades Massif, in Sete Cidades, S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Sete_Cidades_%28panorama%29.JPG/800px-Sete_Cidades_%28panorama%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="800" height="127" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Sete_Cidades_%28panorama%29.JPG/1200px-Sete_Cidades_%28panorama%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Sete_Cidades_%28panorama%29.JPG/1600px-Sete_Cidades_%28panorama%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="10833" data-file-height="1723" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sete_Cidades_(panorama).JPG" title="File:Sete Cidades (panorama).JPG"> </a></div><center>The <a href="/wiki/Lagoa_das_Sete_Cidades" title="Lagoa das Sete Cidades">Lagoa das Sete Cidades</a>, located within the <a href="/wiki/Sete_Cidades_Massif" title="Sete Cidades Massif">Sete Cidades Massif</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Sete_Cidades_(Ponta_Delgada)" title="Sete Cidades (Ponta Delgada)">Sete Cidades</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island" title="S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island">S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island</a>.</center></div></div></div>\n<p>These islands can be divided into three recognizable groups located on the Azores Plateau:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Group,_Azores" title="Eastern Group, Azores">Eastern Group</a> (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">Grupo Oriental</i>) of S\xc3\xa3o Miguel, Santa Maria and Formigas Islets</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Group,_Azores" title="Central Group, Azores">Central Group</a> (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">Grupo Central</i>) of Terceira, Graciosa, S\xc3\xa3o Jorge, Pico and Faial</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Western_Group" title="Western Group">Western Group</a> (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">Grupo Ocidental</i>) of Flores and Corvo.</li></ul>\n<p>Several sub-surface reefs (particularly the <a href="/wiki/Dollabarat" title="Dollabarat">Dollabarat</a> on the fringe of the Formigas), banks (specifically the <a href="/wiki/Princess_Alice_Bank" title="Princess Alice Bank">Princess Alice Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_de_Castro_Bank" title="Dom Jo\xc3\xa3o de Castro Bank">D. Jo\xc3\xa3o de Castro Bank</a>), as well as many <a href="/wiki/Hydrothermal_vents_and_seamounts_of_the_Azores" title="Hydrothermal vents and seamounts of the Azores">hydrothermal vents and sea-mounts</a> are monitored by the regional authorities, owing to the complex geotectonic and socioeconomic significance within the economic exclusion zone of the archipelago.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From a geostructural perspective, the Azores is located above an active <a href="/wiki/Triple_junction" title="Triple junction">triple junction</a> between three of the world\'s major tectonic plates (the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Plate</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian Plate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/African_Plate" title="African Plate">African Plate</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Machado2008p14_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Machado2008p14-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> a condition that has translated into the existence of many faults and fractures in this region of the Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The westernmost islands of the archipelago (Corvo and Flores) are located on the North American Plate, while the remaining islands are located within the boundary that divides the Eurasian and African plates.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The principal tectonic structures that exist in the region of the Azores are the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Ridge" title="Mid-Atlantic Ridge">Mid-Atlantic Ridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Terceira_Rift" title="Terceira Rift">Terceira Rift</a>, the Azores Fracture Zone and the Gl\xc3\xb3ria Fault.<sup id="cite_ref-Machado2008p14_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Machado2008p14-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The Mid-Atlantic Ridge is the main frontier between the North American Plate and the African-Eurasian Plates that crosses the Azores Plateau between the islands of Flores and Faial from north to south then to the southwest; it is an extensive form crossed by many transform faults running perpendicular to its north\xe2\x80\x93south orientation, that is seismically active and susceptible to volcanism.\n</p><p>The Terceira Rift is a system of fractures that extends from the Mid-Atlantic Ridge to the Gl\xc3\xb3ria Fault that represents the main frontier between the Eurasian and African Plates. It is defined by a line of submarine volcanoes and island mounts that extend northwest to southeast for about 550 kilometres (342 miles), from the area west of Graciosa until the islets of the Formigas, that includes the islands of Graciosa, Terceira and S\xc3\xa3o Miguel. Its northwest limit connects to the Mid-Atlantic Ridge, while the southeast section intersects the Gloria Fault southeast of the island of Santa Maria.\n</p><p>The Azores Fracture Zone extends from the Gl\xc3\xb3ria Fault and encompasses a relatively inactive area to the south of the islands of the Central and Eastern groups north to the Terceira Rift, along a 45\xc2\xb0 angle. The Gl\xc3\xb3ria Fault, for its part, extends 800 kilometres (497 miles) along a linear line from the Azores to the <a href="/wiki/Azores%E2%80%93Gibraltar_Transform_Fault" title="Azores\xe2\x80\x93Gibraltar Transform Fault">Azores\xe2\x80\x93Gibraltar Transform Fault</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Furnas,_isla_de_San_Miguel,_Azores,_Portugal,_2020-07-29,_DD_82-90_PAN.jpg" class="image" title="Usual biome of the islands. A mix of laurisilva, introduced Cryptomeria forests and agricultural fields, with usually small populated centers in between. Photo from Furnas, S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Vista_de_Furnas%2C_isla_de_San_Miguel%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal%2C_2020-07-29%2C_DD_82-90_PAN.jpg/800px-Vista_de_Furnas%2C_isla_de_San_Miguel%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal%2C_2020-07-29%2C_DD_82-90_PAN.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="217" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Vista_de_Furnas%2C_isla_de_San_Miguel%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal%2C_2020-07-29%2C_DD_82-90_PAN.jpg/1200px-Vista_de_Furnas%2C_isla_de_San_Miguel%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal%2C_2020-07-29%2C_DD_82-90_PAN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Vista_de_Furnas%2C_isla_de_San_Miguel%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal%2C_2020-07-29%2C_DD_82-90_PAN.jpg/1600px-Vista_de_Furnas%2C_isla_de_San_Miguel%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal%2C_2020-07-29%2C_DD_82-90_PAN.jpg 2x" data-file-width="17803" data-file-height="4836" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Furnas,_isla_de_San_Miguel,_Azores,_Portugal,_2020-07-29,_DD_82-90_PAN.jpg" title="File:Vista de Furnas, isla de San Miguel, Azores, Portugal, 2020-07-29, DD 82-90 PAN.jpg"> </a></div><center>Usual biome of the islands. A mix of laurisilva, introduced <a href="/wiki/Cryptomeria" title="Cryptomeria">Cryptomeria</a> forests and agricultural fields, with usually small populated centers in between. Photo from <a href="/wiki/Furnas" title="Furnas">Furnas</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island" title="S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island">S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island</a></center></div></div></div>\n<p>The island\'s volcanism is associated with the <a href="/wiki/Rift" title="Rift">rifting</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Azores_Triple_Junction" title="Azores Triple Junction">Azores Triple Junction</a>; the spread of the crust along the existing faults and fractures has produced many of the active volcanic and seismic events,<sup id="cite_ref-Ferreira,_2005,_p._4_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferreira,_2005,_p._4-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> while supported by buoyant upwelling in the deeper mantle, some associate with an <a href="/wiki/Azores_hotspot" title="Azores hotspot">Azores hotspot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Most of the volcanic activity has centered, primarily, along the Terceira Rift.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From the beginning of the island\'s settlement, around the 15th century, there have been 28 registered volcanic eruptions (15 terrestrial and 13 submarine). The last significant volcanic eruption, the <a href="/wiki/Capelinhos" title="Capelinhos">Capelinhos</a> volcano (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">Vulc\xc3\xa3o dos Capelinhos</i>), occurred off the coast of the island of Faial in 1957; the most recent volcanic activity occurred in the seamounts and submarine volcanoes off the coast of Serreta and in the Pico-S\xc3\xa3o Jorge Channel.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pico-HortaFaial_(crop).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Pico-HortaFaial_%28crop%29.jpg/220px-Pico-HortaFaial_%28crop%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Pico-HortaFaial_%28crop%29.jpg/330px-Pico-HortaFaial_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Pico-HortaFaial_%28crop%29.jpg/440px-Pico-HortaFaial_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="755" data-file-height="503" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pico-HortaFaial_(crop).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Pico" title="Mount Pico">Mount Pico</a>, on Pico Island, is the highest peak in all of Portugal.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Path_to_Po%C3%A7o_da_Alagoinha,_Flores,_Azores,_Portugal_(PPL2-Enhanced)_4_julesvernex2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Path_to_Po%C3%A7o_da_Alagoinha%2C_Flores%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_4_julesvernex2.jpg/220px-Path_to_Po%C3%A7o_da_Alagoinha%2C_Flores%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_4_julesvernex2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Path_to_Po%C3%A7o_da_Alagoinha%2C_Flores%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_4_julesvernex2.jpg/330px-Path_to_Po%C3%A7o_da_Alagoinha%2C_Flores%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_4_julesvernex2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Path_to_Po%C3%A7o_da_Alagoinha%2C_Flores%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_4_julesvernex2.jpg/440px-Path_to_Po%C3%A7o_da_Alagoinha%2C_Flores%2C_Azores%2C_Portugal_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_4_julesvernex2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5981" data-file-height="3987" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Path_to_Po%C3%A7o_da_Alagoinha,_Flores,_Azores,_Portugal_(PPL2-Enhanced)_4_julesvernex2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Laurel_forest#Macaronesia_and_the_Mediterranean_Basin" title="Laurel forest">Macaronesian Laurisilva forest</a> on Flores Island</div></div></div>\n<p>The islands have many examples of volcano-built geomorphology including caves and <a href="/wiki/Lava_tube" title="Lava tube">lava tubes</a> (such as the <a href="/wiki/Gruta_das_Torres" title="Gruta das Torres">Gruta das Torres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o" title="Algar do Carv\xc3\xa3o">Algar do Carv\xc3\xa3o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gruta_do_Natal" title="Gruta do Natal">Gruta do Natal</a>, Gruta das Cinco Ribeiras), the coastal lava fields (like the coast of <a href="/wiki/Feteiras" title="Feteiras">Feteiras</a>, Faial, the Mist\xc3\xa9rio of <a href="/wiki/Prainha_(S%C3%A3o_Roque_do_Pico)" title="Prainha (S\xc3\xa3o Roque do Pico)">Prainha</a> or S\xc3\xa3o Jo\xc3\xa3o on Pico Island) in addition to the inactive cones in central S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island, the aforementioned Capelinhos on Faial, the volcanic complexes of Terceira or <a href="/wiki/Plinian_eruption" title="Plinian eruption">Plinian</a> caldeira of Corvo Island.\nThe islands of the archipelago were formed through volcanic and seismic activity during the <a href="/wiki/Neogene" title="Neogene">Neogene</a> Period; the first embryonic surfaces started to appear in the waters of Santa Maria during the <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene epoch</a> (from circa 8&#160;million years ago). \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caldeira_Faial_ca_580_m.%C3%BC.NN._Kesselboden.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Caldeira_Faial_ca_580_m.%C3%BC.NN._Kesselboden.JPG/220px-Caldeira_Faial_ca_580_m.%C3%BC.NN._Kesselboden.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Caldeira_Faial_ca_580_m.%C3%BC.NN._Kesselboden.JPG/330px-Caldeira_Faial_ca_580_m.%C3%BC.NN._Kesselboden.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Caldeira_Faial_ca_580_m.%C3%BC.NN._Kesselboden.JPG/440px-Caldeira_Faial_ca_580_m.%C3%BC.NN._Kesselboden.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3584" data-file-height="2016" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caldeira_Faial_ca_580_m.%C3%BC.NN._Kesselboden.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">Caldeira</a></i> on Faial Island</div></div></div>\n<p>The sequence of the island formation has been generally characterized as: Santa Maria (8.12 Ma), S\xc3\xa3o Miguel (4.1 Ma), Terceira (3.52 Ma), Graciosa (2.5 Ma), Flores (2.16 Ma), Faial (0.7 Ma), S\xc3\xa3o Jorge (0.55 Ma), Corvo (0.7 Ma) and the youngest, Pico (0.27 Ma).<sup id="cite_ref-Carine,_2010,_p._78_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carine,_2010,_p._78-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Although all islands have experienced volcanism during their geological history, within recorded "human settlement" history the islands of Santa Maria, Graciosa, Flores, and Corvo have not experienced any volcanic eruptions; in addition to active fumaroles and hot-springs, the remaining islands have had sporadic eruptions since the 14th century. Apart from the Capelinhos volcano in 1957\xe2\x80\x9358, the last recorded instance of "island formation" occurred off the coast of S\xc3\xa3o Miguel, when the island of <a href="/wiki/Sabrina_Island_(Azores)" title="Sabrina Island (Azores)">Sabrina</a> was briefly formed.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o_-_Portugal_(236262316).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o_-_Portugal_%28236262316%29.jpg/220px-Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o_-_Portugal_%28236262316%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o_-_Portugal_%28236262316%29.jpg/330px-Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o_-_Portugal_%28236262316%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o_-_Portugal_%28236262316%29.jpg/440px-Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o_-_Portugal_%28236262316%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o_-_Portugal_(236262316).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Algar_do_Carv%C3%A3o" title="Algar do Carv\xc3\xa3o">Algar do Carv\xc3\xa3o</a> volcanic cave on Terceira Island</div></div></div>\n<p>Owing to its geodynamic environment, the region has been a center of intense seismic activity, particularly along its tectonic boundaries on the Mid-Atlantic Ridge and Terceira Rift. Seismic events although frequent, are usually tectonic or vulco-tectonic in nature, but in general are of low to medium intensities, occasionally punctuated by events of level 5 or greater on the <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">Richter magnitude scale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The most severe earthquake was registered in 1757, near <a href="/wiki/Calheta,_Azores" title="Calheta, Azores">Calheta</a> on the island of S\xc3\xa3o Jorge, which exceeded 7 on the Richter magnitude scale. In comparison, the 1522 earthquake that was mentioned by historian <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Frutuoso" title="Gaspar Frutuoso">Gaspar Frutuoso</a> measured 6.8, but its effects were judged to be X (<i>Extreme</i>) on the <a href="/wiki/Modified_Mercalli_intensity_scale" title="Modified Mercalli intensity scale">Mercalli intensity scale</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and was responsible for the destruction of <a href="/wiki/Vila_Franca_do_Campo" title="Vila Franca do Campo">Vila Franca do Campo</a> and landslides that may have killed more than 5,000 of the inhabitants.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fogo_lake_-_S.Miguel_island_-_Azores_(39000072215)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Fogo_lake_-_S.Miguel_island_-_Azores_%2839000072215%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Fogo_lake_-_S.Miguel_island_-_Azores_%2839000072215%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Fogo_lake_-_S.Miguel_island_-_Azores_%2839000072215%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Fogo_lake_-_S.Miguel_island_-_Azores_%2839000072215%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Fogo_lake_-_S.Miguel_island_-_Azores_%2839000072215%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Fogo_lake_-_S.Miguel_island_-_Azores_%2839000072215%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1174" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fogo_lake_-_S.Miguel_island_-_Azores_(39000072215)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lagoa_do_Fogo" title="Lagoa do Fogo">Fogo lake</a> on S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biome">Biome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Biome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A%C3%A7ores_2010-07-20_(5081868308).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/A%C3%A7ores_2010-07-20_%285081868308%29.jpg/170px-A%C3%A7ores_2010-07-20_%285081868308%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/A%C3%A7ores_2010-07-20_%285081868308%29.jpg/255px-A%C3%A7ores_2010-07-20_%285081868308%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/A%C3%A7ores_2010-07-20_%285081868308%29.jpg/340px-A%C3%A7ores_2010-07-20_%285081868308%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="4068" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A%C3%A7ores_2010-07-20_(5081868308).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Faj%C3%A3_dos_Cubres" title="Faj\xc3\xa3 dos Cubres">Faj\xc3\xa3 dos Cubres</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Calheta,_Azores" title="Calheta, Azores">Calheta</a>, S\xc3\xa3o Jorge Island, is one of many <i><a href="/wiki/Faj%C3%A3" title="Faj\xc3\xa3">faj\xc3\xa3s</a></i> (ancient lava overflows) in the Azores.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pico_da_S%C3%A9,_Inverno_de_2008,_ilha_das_Flores,_A%C3%A7ores.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pico_da_S%C3%A9%2C_Inverno_de_2008%2C_ilha_das_Flores%2C_A%C3%A7ores.JPG/220px-Pico_da_S%C3%A9%2C_Inverno_de_2008%2C_ilha_das_Flores%2C_A%C3%A7ores.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pico_da_S%C3%A9%2C_Inverno_de_2008%2C_ilha_das_Flores%2C_A%C3%A7ores.JPG/330px-Pico_da_S%C3%A9%2C_Inverno_de_2008%2C_ilha_das_Flores%2C_A%C3%A7ores.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pico_da_S%C3%A9%2C_Inverno_de_2008%2C_ilha_das_Flores%2C_A%C3%A7ores.JPG/440px-Pico_da_S%C3%A9%2C_Inverno_de_2008%2C_ilha_das_Flores%2C_A%C3%A7ores.JPG 2x" data-file-width="980" data-file-height="735" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pico_da_S%C3%A9,_Inverno_de_2008,_ilha_das_Flores,_A%C3%A7ores.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pico_da_S%C3%A9" class="extiw" title="pt:Pico da S\xc3\xa9">Pico da S\xc3\xa9</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cedros_(Santa_Cruz_das_Flores)" title="Cedros (Santa Cruz das Flores)">Cedros</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The archipelago lies in the <a href="/wiki/Palearctic_realm" title="Palearctic realm">Palearctic realm</a> and has a unique biotic community that includes the <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesian</a> <a href="/wiki/Subtropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical">subtropical</a> <a href="/wiki/Laurel_forest" title="Laurel forest">laurissilva</a>, with many <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic species</a> of plants and animals.<sup id="cite_ref-Kostas2010_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kostas2010-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Species_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Species-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> There are at least 6,112 terrestrial species, of which about 411 are <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a>. The majority (75%) of these endemics are animals, mostly <a href="/wiki/Arthropod" title="Arthropod">arthropods</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mollusca" title="Mollusca">mollusks</a>. New species are found regularly in the Azores (e.g., 30 different new species of land snails were discovered circa 2013<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montanha_do_Pico,_aspectos_5_ilha_do_Pico,_A%C3%A7ores,_Portugal.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Montanha_do_Pico%2C_aspectos_5_ilha_do_Pico%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal.JPG/220px-Montanha_do_Pico%2C_aspectos_5_ilha_do_Pico%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Montanha_do_Pico%2C_aspectos_5_ilha_do_Pico%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal.JPG/330px-Montanha_do_Pico%2C_aspectos_5_ilha_do_Pico%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Montanha_do_Pico%2C_aspectos_5_ilha_do_Pico%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal.JPG/440px-Montanha_do_Pico%2C_aspectos_5_ilha_do_Pico%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montanha_do_Pico,_aspectos_5_ilha_do_Pico,_A%C3%A7ores,_Portugal.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pico Island landscape</div></div></div>\n<p>Even though the Azores look very green and sometimes wild, the vegetation has been extremely altered. A great part of it has been wiped out in the past 600 years for its valuable wood (for tools, buildings, boats, fire wood, and so on) and to clear land for agriculture. As a result, it is estimated that more than half of insects on the Graciosa island have disappeared or will become extinct.<sup id="cite_ref-Kostas2010_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kostas2010-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Many cultivated places (which are traditionally dedicated to pasture or to growing <a href="/wiki/Colocasia" title="Colocasia">colocasia</a>, potatoes, maize and other crops) have now been abandoned, especially as a result of emigration. Consequently, some <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive</a> plants have filled these deserted and disturbed lands. <a href="/wiki/Hydrangea" title="Hydrangea">Hydrangeas</a> are another potential pest, but their threat is less serious. Notwithstanding the fact that hydrangeas were introduced from America or Asia, some locals consider them a symbol of the archipelago and propagate them along roadsides. <i><a href="/wiki/Cryptomeria" title="Cryptomeria">Cryptomeria</a></i>, the Japanese cedar, is a <a href="/wiki/Conifer" title="Conifer">conifer</a> extensively grown for its timber. The two most common of these alien species are <i><a href="/wiki/Pittosporum_undulatum" title="Pittosporum undulatum">Pittosporum undulatum</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hedychium_gardnerianum" title="Hedychium gardnerianum">Hedychium gardnerianum</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Reforestation efforts with native <a href="/wiki/Laurel_forest" title="Laurel forest">laurissilva</a> vegetation have been accomplished successfully in many parts of the Azores.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilheu_de_la_Ballena,_Ponta_da_Barca_(6061369383)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Ilheu_de_la_Ballena%2C_Ponta_da_Barca_%286061369383%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Ilheu_de_la_Ballena%2C_Ponta_da_Barca_%286061369383%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Ilheu_de_la_Ballena%2C_Ponta_da_Barca_%286061369383%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Ilheu_de_la_Ballena%2C_Ponta_da_Barca_%286061369383%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Ilheu_de_la_Ballena%2C_Ponta_da_Barca_%286061369383%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Ilheu_de_la_Ballena%2C_Ponta_da_Barca_%286061369383%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2107" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilheu_de_la_Ballena,_Ponta_da_Barca_(6061369383)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilh%C3%A9u_da_Baleia" class="extiw" title="pt:Ilh\xc3\xa9u da Baleia">Ilh\xc3\xa9u da Baleia</a> islet near Graciosa Island</div></div></div>\n<p>The Azores has at least two endemic living bird species. The <a href="/wiki/Azores_bullfinch" title="Azores bullfinch">Azores bullfinch</a>, or <i>Priolo</i>, is restricted to remnant laurisilva forest in the mountains at the eastern end of S\xc3\xa3o Miguel<sup id="cite_ref-AzoresforestsWWF_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AzoresforestsWWF-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and is classified by BirdLife International as <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a>. <a href="/wiki/Monteiro%27s_storm_petrel" title="Monteiro&#39;s storm petrel">Monteiro\'s storm petrel</a>, described to science as recently as 2008, is known to breed in just two locations in the islands but may occur more widely. An extinct species of owl, the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Miguel_scops_owl" title="S\xc3\xa3o Miguel scops owl">S\xc3\xa3o Miguel scops owl</a>, has recently been described, which probably became extinct after human settlement because of habitat destruction and the introduction of alien species. Five species of flightless <a href="/wiki/Rail_(bird)" title="Rail (bird)">rail</a> once existed on the islands, as did a flightless quail<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and another species of bullfinch, but these also went extinct after human colonization. Eleven subspecies of bird are endemic to the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-zt_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zt-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Azores has an endemic bat, the <a href="/wiki/Azores_noctule" title="Azores noctule">Azores noctule</a>, which has an unusually high frequency of diurnal flight.\n</p><p>The islets of the Formigas (the Portuguese word for "ants"), including the area known as the <a href="/wiki/Dollabarat" title="Dollabarat">Dollabarat</a> Reef, have a rich environment of maritime species, such as <a href="/wiki/Black_coral" title="Black coral">black coral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manta_ray" title="Manta ray">manta rays</a>, different species of sharks, whales, and sea turtles. Seventeen new marine reserves (with special conservation status) were added to the Azorean Marine Park (which covers around 900.000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (347.492&#160;sq&#160;mi)).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On S\xc3\xa3o Miguel there are notable micro-habitats formed by hot springs that host <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">extremophile</a> microorganisms.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Porto_das_Cinco,_freguesia_das_Cinco_Ribeiras,_Ilha_Terceira,_A%C3%A7ores.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Porto_das_Cinco%2C_freguesia_das_Cinco_Ribeiras%2C_Ilha_Terceira%2C_A%C3%A7ores.jpg/220px-Porto_das_Cinco%2C_freguesia_das_Cinco_Ribeiras%2C_Ilha_Terceira%2C_A%C3%A7ores.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Porto_das_Cinco%2C_freguesia_das_Cinco_Ribeiras%2C_Ilha_Terceira%2C_A%C3%A7ores.jpg/330px-Porto_das_Cinco%2C_freguesia_das_Cinco_Ribeiras%2C_Ilha_Terceira%2C_A%C3%A7ores.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Porto_das_Cinco%2C_freguesia_das_Cinco_Ribeiras%2C_Ilha_Terceira%2C_A%C3%A7ores.jpg/440px-Porto_das_Cinco%2C_freguesia_das_Cinco_Ribeiras%2C_Ilha_Terceira%2C_A%C3%A7ores.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Porto_das_Cinco,_freguesia_das_Cinco_Ribeiras,_Ilha_Terceira,_A%C3%A7ores.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cinco_Ribeiras" title="Cinco Ribeiras">Cinco Ribeiras</a> coast on <a href="/wiki/Terceira_Island" title="Terceira Island">Terceira</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The archipelago is spread out at roughly the same latitude as the southern half of mainland Portugal, giving it a generally tepid, oceanic, warm subtropical climate, with mild annual oscillations. Daily maximum temperatures at low altitudes usually range between 16 and 25&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61 and 77&#160;\xc2\xb0F). The average annual rainfall increases from east to west, ranging from 700&#160;mm (28&#160;in) in Santa Maria to 1,600&#160;mm (63&#160;in) in Flores and reaching 6,300 millimetres (250&#160;in) on Mount Pico.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_of_the_Azores_islands_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_of_the_Azores_islands-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Azores_High" title="Azores High">Azores High</a>, an area of high <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">atmospheric pressure</a>, is named after the islands. Under the K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification, the eastern group is usually classified as <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean Climate">Mediterranean</a> while the central and western group is increasingly more <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical</a> because of the effects of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azores_flores_ribeira_grande.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Azores_flores_ribeira_grande.jpg/220px-Azores_flores_ribeira_grande.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Azores_flores_ribeira_grande.jpg/330px-Azores_flores_ribeira_grande.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Azores_flores_ribeira_grande.jpg/440px-Azores_flores_ribeira_grande.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azores_flores_ribeira_grande.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Waterfalls on Flores</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azores_7166_(7813296310)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Azores_7166_%287813296310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Azores_7166_%287813296310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Azores_7166_%287813296310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Azores_7166_%287813296310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Azores_7166_%287813296310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Azores_7166_%287813296310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1472" data-file-height="741" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azores_7166_(7813296310)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a
