href="/wiki/Hydrangea" title="Hydrangea">Hydrangeas</a> on Faial</div></div></div>\n<p>Salvador Rivas-Mart\xc3\xadnez data presents several different bioclimatic zones for the Azores.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Seasonal_lag" title="Seasonal lag">Seasonal lag</a> is extreme in the low-sun half of the year, with December being milder than April regarding mean temperatures. Although temperatures as warm as 32.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (89.8&#160;\xc2\xb0F) have been recorded on Pico, neither Ponta Delgada nor Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo, the two largest cities, have ever gone above 30&#160;\xc2\xb0C (86&#160;\xc2\xb0F).\n</p><p>The Azores have the warmest winters in Europe. During summer the lag is somewhat lower, with August being the warmest month, though September is usually as warm or warmer than July. There has never been a frost, snowfall, freeze or even temperatures below 5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (41&#160;\xc2\xb0F) recorded at sea level on any of the islands. The coldest weather in winter usually comes from northwesterly <a href="/wiki/Air_mass" title="Air mass">air masses</a> originating from <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador</a> in Canada. However, since those air masses are warmed up as they pass across the warmer Atlantic Ocean, temperatures by day even then exceed 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). The westernmost islands of the archipelago, namely Flores and Corvo, get the strongest maritime moderation and the most rainfall since both are right on the Gulf Stream waters.\n</p><p>The average <a href="/wiki/Relative_humidity" class="mw-redirect" title="Relative humidity">relative humidity</a> can range from 80% at the coast and 90% at higher elevations. Summers are especially humid in August and may increase the perceived temperature by a few degrees. Winters are not only very mild but also very humid and as so are relatively comfortable, though rainy.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Instituto_de_Meteorologia" class="mw-redirect" title="Instituto de Meteorologia">Instituto de Meteorologia</a> has identified the following weather extremes:<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Highest minimum air temperature: 24.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (75.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F), in <a href="/wiki/Angra_do_Hero%C3%ADsmo" title="Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo">Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo</a>, Terceira (30 June 1996)</li>\n<li>Lowest minimum air temperature: \xe2\x88\x923.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (25.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F), in Ch\xc3\xa3 das Lagoinhas, S\xc3\xa3o Jorge (2 January 1973)</li>\n<li>Highest maximum air temperature: 32.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (89.8&#160;\xc2\xb0F), in <a href="/wiki/Madalena,_Azores" title="Madalena, Azores">Madalena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pico_(Azores)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pico (Azores)">Pico</a> (7 September 1985)</li>\n<li>Lowest maximum air temperature: 4.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (39.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F), Ch\xc3\xa3 das Lagoinhas, S\xc3\xa3o Jorge (20 February 1972)</li>\n<li>Maximum precipitation in 24 hours: 276&#160;mm (10.87&#160;in), <a href="/wiki/Furnas" title="Furnas">Furnas</a>, S\xc3\xa3o Miguel (3 October 1974)</li>\n<li>Maximum wind speed: &gt;176&#160;km/hour, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_Island" title="Santa Maria Island">Santa Maria</a>, (15 December 1989)</li></ul>\n<table class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in \xc2\xb0F</td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in inches</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricanes">Hurricanes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hurricanes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Azores_hurricanes" title="List of Azores hurricanes">List of Azores hurricanes</a></div>\n<p>The Azores are known for small hurricanes. A total of 14 <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical</a> or <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical cyclones</a> have affected the region in history. Most of them were either <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical storms</a> when they affected the region, although several <a href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_hurricane_scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir-Simpson hurricane scale">Category 1 hurricanes</a> have reached the Azores. Only one major hurricane has ever impacted the Azores; <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ophelia_(2017)" title="Hurricane Ophelia (2017)">Hurricane Ophelia</a> in 2017, at Category 3 intensity. The following storms have impacted the region while at Category 1 strength: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fran_(1973)" title="Hurricane Fran (1973)">Hurricane Fran</a> in 1973, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Emmy" title="Hurricane Emmy">Hurricane Emmy</a> in 1976, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gordon_(2006)" title="Hurricane Gordon (2006)">Hurricane Gordon</a> in 2006, <a href="/wiki/2012_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Gordon" title="2012 Atlantic hurricane season">Hurricane Gordon</a> in 2012 and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Alex_(2016)" title="Hurricane Alex (2016)">Hurricane Alex</a> in 2016. Several tropical storms have hit the region, including <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Irma_(1978)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Storm Irma (1978)">Tropical Storm Irma</a> in 1978, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bonnie_(1992)" title="Hurricane Bonnie (1992)">Hurricane Bonnie</a> in 1992, <a href="/wiki/1992_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Charley" title="1992 Atlantic hurricane season">Hurricane Charley</a> in 1992, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Erika_(1997)" title="Hurricane Erika (1997)">Hurricane Erika</a> in 1997, and <a href="/wiki/2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Gaston" title="2016 Atlantic hurricane season">Hurricane Gaston</a> in 2016. Storms that were extratropical when they impacted the region include <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Tanya_(1995)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Tanya (1995)">Hurricane Tanya</a> in 1995, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)">Tropical Storm Ana</a> in 2003 and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Grace_(2009)" title="Tropical Storm Grace (2009)">Tropical Storm Grace</a> in 2009. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/2005_Azores_subtropical_storm" title="2005 Azores subtropical storm">2005 Azores subtropical storm</a> affected the region in October 2005.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In order of importance, the main sectors of employment of the Azores are services, agriculture, fishery, industry and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Azores are divided into 19 municipalities (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">concelhos</i>); each municipality is further divided into <i><a href="/wiki/Freguesia" title="Freguesia">freguesias</a></i> (civil administrative parishes), of which there is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_parishes_of_Portugal" title="List of parishes of Portugal">total of 156</a> in all of the Azores.\n</p><p>There are six cities (Portuguese: <i>cidades</i>) in the Azores: <a href="/wiki/Ponta_Delgada" title="Ponta Delgada">Ponta Delgada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lagoa_(Azores)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lagoa (Azores)">Lagoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ribeira_Grande,_S%C3%A3o_Miguel" class="mw-redirect" title="Ribeira Grande, S\xc3\xa3o Miguel">Ribeira Grande</a> on the island of S\xc3\xa3o Miguel; <a href="/wiki/Angra_do_Hero%C3%ADsmo" title="Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo">Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Praia_da_Vit%C3%B3ria" title="Praia da Vit\xc3\xb3ria">Praia da Vit\xc3\xb3ria</a> on the island of Terceira, and <a href="/wiki/Horta_(Azores)" class="mw-redirect" title="Horta (Azores)">Horta</a> on Faial. Three of these, <a href="/wiki/Ponta_Delgada" title="Ponta Delgada">Ponta Delgada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angra_(Azores)" class="mw-redirect" title="Angra (Azores)">Angra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horta_(Azores)" class="mw-redirect" title="Horta (Azores)">Horta</a> are considered <a href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (political)">capital/administrative cities</a> to the regional government: homes to the President (Ponta Delgada), the Judiciary (Angra) and the Regional Assembly (Horta). Angra also serves as the ecclesiastical centre of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Angra" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Angra">Roman Catholic Diocese of Angra</a>, the episcopal see of the Azores.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:95%; margin:1em auto 1em auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="2" style="width:100pt;">Island</th>\n<th rowspan="2" style="text-align:right;">242,823</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">19</td>\n<td></td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilha_de_S%C3%A3o_Miguel_DSC00659_(36586155410)_(cropped)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ponta Delgada, on S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island, is the largest city in the Azores and the executive capital of the Azores.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angra_do_heroismo_garden_view_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Angra_do_heroismo_garden_view_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Angra_do_heroismo_garden_view_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Angra_do_heroismo_garden_view_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Angra_do_heroismo_garden_view_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Angra_do_heroismo_garden_view_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Angra_do_heroismo_garden_view_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4347" data-file-height="1926" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Angra_do_heroismo_garden_view_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo, on Terceira Island, is <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage">UNESCO World Heritage</a> and the judicial capital of the Azores.</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the 2019 Census, population in the Azores was 242,796.<sup id="cite_ref-ine2019_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ine2019-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The Azores were uninhabited when Portuguese navigators arrived in the early 15th century; settlement began in 1439 with migrants from several regions of mainland Portugal and from <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>. Many Portuguese Sephardic Jews settled on the islands in large numbers. The islands were also settled by Moorish prisoners and African slaves from Guinea, Cape Verde and S\xc3\xa3o Tom\xc3\xa9. Flemish, French, and Galicians contributed to the initial settlement. Thus the Azorean population received a significant contribution from people with genetic backgrounds other than Portuguese.\n</p><p>\nThe nature of the economy dictated that <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slavery</a> never became common in the Azores because the slaves were sent to Brazil and the Caribbean. Only a few remained in the Azores for forced labor such as domestic chores, although the islands sometimes served as a waypoint for ships carrying <a href="/wiki/History_of_slavery" title="History of slavery">African slaves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colonialism:_An_International,_Social,_Cultural,_and_Political_Encyclopedia_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colonialism:_An_International,_Social,_Cultural,_and_Political_Encyclopedia-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Africans, Moors, Jews, Scots, Germans, Italians, French, Spanish, Flemish, and Portuguese all migrated to the Azores.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cidade_da_Horta_vista_da_Ba%C3%ADa_da_Horta,_ilha_do_Faial,_A%C3%A7ores,_Portugal_(cropped).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Cidade_da_Horta_vista_da_Ba%C3%ADa_da_Horta%2C_ilha_do_Faial%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG/220px-Cidade_da_Horta_vista_da_Ba%C3%ADa_da_Horta%2C_ilha_do_Faial%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Cidade_da_Horta_vista_da_Ba%C3%ADa_da_Horta%2C_ilha_do_Faial%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG/330px-Cidade_da_Horta_vista_da_Ba%C3%ADa_da_Horta%2C_ilha_do_Faial%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Cidade_da_Horta_vista_da_Ba%C3%ADa_da_Horta%2C_ilha_do_Faial%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG/440px-Cidade_da_Horta_vista_da_Ba%C3%ADa_da_Horta%2C_ilha_do_Faial%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3499" data-file-height="1627" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cidade_da_Horta_vista_da_Ba%C3%ADa_da_Horta,_ilha_do_Faial,_A%C3%A7ores,_Portugal_(cropped).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Horta, on Faial Island, is the legislative capital of the Azores.</div></div></div><p>\nAs in continental Portugal, the most frequent <a href="/wiki/Human_mitochondrial_DNA_haplogroup" title="Human mitochondrial DNA haplogroup">mtDNA haplogroup</a> in the Azores is <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_H_(mtDNA)" title="Haplogroup H (mtDNA)">H</a> (45.2%), followed by <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_U_(mtDNA)" title="Haplogroup U (mtDNA)">U</a> (16.7%), <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_T_(mtDNA)" title="Haplogroup T (mtDNA)">T</a> (10.1%), <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_K_(mtDNA)" title="Haplogroup K (mtDNA)">K</a> (6.5%), <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_pre-HV_(mtDNA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup pre-HV (mtDNA)">pre-HV</a> clades (5.6%) and a smaller African <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_L1_(mtDNA)" title="Haplogroup L1 (mtDNA)">L haplogroups</a> frequency (3.4%) than in Madeira. Inhabitants of the various islands have DNA of various origins.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> A minority on the islands has non-European ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-Brehm2003_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brehm2003-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manuel_Gaspar,_moinho_t%C3%ADpico,_Santa_Cruz_da_Graciosa,_ilha_Graciosa,_A%C3%A7ores,_Portugal_(cropped).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Manuel_Gaspar%2C_moinho_t%C3%ADpico%2C_Santa_Cruz_da_Graciosa%2C_ilha_Graciosa%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG/220px-Manuel_Gaspar%2C_moinho_t%C3%ADpico%2C_Santa_Cruz_da_Graciosa%2C_ilha_Graciosa%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Manuel_Gaspar%2C_moinho_t%C3%ADpico%2C_Santa_Cruz_da_Graciosa%2C_ilha_Graciosa%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG/330px-Manuel_Gaspar%2C_moinho_t%C3%ADpico%2C_Santa_Cruz_da_Graciosa%2C_ilha_Graciosa%2C_A%C3%A7ores%2C_Portugal_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2453" data-file-height="2472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manuel_Gaspar,_moinho_t%C3%ADpico,_Santa_Cruz_da_Graciosa,_ilha_Graciosa,_A%C3%A7ores,_Portugal_(cropped).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Flemish_people" title="Flemish people">Flemish settlers</a> built windmills like this one on Graciosa Island.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emigration">Emigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Emigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since the 17th century, many Azoreans have emigrated, mainly to Brazil, Uruguay, the United States and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a> and southeastern <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> are the primary destination for Azorean emigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> From 1921 to 1977, about 250,000 Azoreans immigrated to Rhode Island and Massachusetts.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Northern <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> was the final destination for many of the Massachusetts immigrants who then moved on to the <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley" title="San Joaquin Valley">San Joaquin Valley</a>, especially the city of <a href="/wiki/Turlock,_California" title="Turlock, California">Turlock</a>. In the late 19th century many Azoreans <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_immigration_to_Hawaii" title="Portuguese immigration to Hawaii">immigrated to the Hawaiian islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-diaspora_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diaspora-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a> fishing industry drew a significant number of Azoreans to the <a href="/wiki/Point_Loma,_San_Diego" title="Point Loma, San Diego">Point Loma</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a> of the early 21st century, Portugal was in a recession from 2011 until 2013, which resulted in high levels of unemployment across the mainland as well as the Azores.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The Great Recession led to an increase of emigration from the Azores.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Florian%C3%B3polis" title="Florian\xc3\xb3polis">Florian\xc3\xb3polis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a> in the <a href="/wiki/South_Region,_Brazil" title="South Region, Brazil">Southern Region</a> of Brazil were founded by Azoreans, who accounted for over half of <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">Santa Catarina</a>\'s populations in the late 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> As late as 1960, mass immigration currents were registered to Brazil, and many were from the Azores.<sup id="cite_ref-diaspora_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diaspora-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_the_Azores" title="Political status of the Azores">Political status of the Azores</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_Santana_(14826301491)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Palacio_de_Santana_%2814826301491%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Palacio_de_Santana_%2814826301491%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-height="614" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_Santana_(14826301491)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_de_Sant%27Ana" class="extiw" title="pt:Pal\xc3\xa1cio de Sant&#39;Ana">Sant\'Ana Palace</a> is the seat of the President of the Azores.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Igr_n_sra_carmo_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Igr_n_sra_carmo_2.JPG/220px-Igr_n_sra_carmo_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Igr_n_sra_carmo_2.JPG/330px-Igr_n_sra_carmo_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Igr_n_sra_carmo_2.JPG/440px-Igr_n_sra_carmo_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3045" data-file-height="2439" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Igr_n_sra_carmo_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Capit%C3%A3es-Generais_(Angra_do_Hero%C3%ADsmo)" class="extiw" title="pt:Pal\xc3\xa1cio dos Capit\xc3\xa3es-Generais (Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo)">Palace of the Capit\xc3\xa3es-Generais</a> is a residence of the Azorean President.</div></div></div><p>\nSince 1976, the Azores has been an autonomous region integrated within the framework of the Portuguese Republic. It has its own government and autonomous legislature within its own political-administrative statute and organic law. Its governmental organs include: the legislative assembly, a <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> parliament composed of 52 elected deputies, elected by universal <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> for a four-year term; the regional government and presidency, with parliamentary legitimacy, composed of a president, a vice-president and seven regional secretaries responsible for day-to-day operations. It is represented in the Council of Ministers by a representative appointed by the president of the Republic, which was created during the revision of the constitution of 2004 (which, among other things, removed the older Portuguese representative that was appointed by the president of the Republic, beholden to the Council of State and coincident with the president). Since becoming a Portuguese autonomous region, the executive branch of the regional authority has been located in <a href="/wiki/Ponta_Delgada" title="Ponta Delgada">Ponta Delgada</a>, the legislative branch in <a href="/wiki/Horta,_Azores" title="Horta, Azores">Horta</a>, and the judicial branch in <a href="/wiki/Angra_do_Hero%C3%ADsmo" title="Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo">Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo</a>.</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solarmadrededeus2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Solarmadrededeus2.JPG/220px-Solarmadrededeus2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Solarmadrededeus2.JPG/330px-Solarmadrededeus2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Solarmadrededeus2.JPG/440px-Solarmadrededeus2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="530" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solarmadrededeus2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Madre_de_Deus_Manor" title="Madre de Deus Manor">Madre de Deus Manor</a> is the seat of the <a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Representante_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_nos_A%C3%A7ores" class="extiw" title="pt:Representante da Rep\xc3\xbablica nos A\xc3\xa7ores">Representative of the Republic</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Largo_2_de_Mar%C3%A7o,_Ponta_Delgada_(16863454855)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Largo_2_de_Mar%C3%A7o%2C_Ponta_Delgada_%2816863454855%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Largo_2_de_Mar%C3%A7o%2C_Ponta_Delgada_%2816863454855%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Largo_2_de_Mar%C3%A7o%2C_Ponta_Delgada_%2816863454855%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Largo_2_de_Mar%C3%A7o%2C_Ponta_Delgada_%2816863454855%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Largo_2_de_Mar%C3%A7o%2C_Ponta_Delgada_%2816863454855%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Largo_2_de_Mar%C3%A7o%2C_Ponta_Delgada_%2816863454855%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2124" data-file-height="1061" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Largo_2_de_Mar%C3%A7o,_Ponta_Delgada_(16863454855)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Palace,_Ponta_Delgada" title="Concei\xc3\xa7\xc3\xa3o Palace, Ponta Delgada">Concei\xc3\xa7\xc3\xa3o Palace</a> is the headquarters of the Azorean cabinet.</div></div></div>\n<p>The islands of the archipelago do not have independent status in law, except in electoral law and are governed by 19 municipalities that subdivide the islands. In addition, until the administrative reform of the 19th century, the following civil parishes had municipal standing: Topo (today integrated into the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Calheta_(Azores)" class="mw-redirect" title="Calheta (Azores)">Calheta</a>, S\xc3\xa3o Jorge); <a href="/wiki/Praia_(Santa_Cruz_da_Graciosa)" title="Praia (Santa Cruz da Graciosa)">Praia</a> (today integrated into municipality of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_da_Graciosa" title="Santa Cruz da Graciosa">Santa Cruz da Graciosa</a>); <a href="/wiki/Vila_de_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o" title="Vila de S\xc3\xa3o Sebasti\xc3\xa3o">S\xc3\xa3o Sebasti\xc3\xa3o</a> (today an integral part of the municipality of Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo); Capelas (now part of the municipality of Ponta Delgada); and \xc3\x81gua de Pau (now a civil parish in the municipality of Lagoa). These civil parishes still retain their titles of "vila" in name only; the populations of Capelas and neighbouring parish still protest the change and promote the restoration of their status. The municipalities are further subdivided into several civil parishes, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Corvo_(Azores)" class="mw-redirect" title="Corvo (Azores)">Corvo</a> (the only municipality by law without a civil parish, owing to its size).\n</p><p>Azorean politics is dominated by the two largest Portuguese political parties, the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(Portugal)" title="Socialist Party (Portugal)">Socialist Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_(Portugal)" title="Social Democratic Party (Portugal)">Social Democratic Party</a>, the former holding a majority in the Legislative Assembly. The <a href="/wiki/CDS_%E2%80%93_People%27s_Party" title="CDS \xe2\x80\x93 People&#39;s Party">Democratic and Social Center / People\'s Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Left_Bloc_(Portugal)" title="Left Bloc (Portugal)">Left Bloc</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Unitary_Democratic_Coalition" title="Unitary Democratic Coalition">Unitary Democratic Coalition</a> and the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Monarchist_Party_(Portugal)" title="People&#39;s Monarchist Party (Portugal)">People\'s Monarchist Party</a> are also represented. As of the 2020 regional election<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the President of the Azores is Social Democratic Party leader <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Bolieiro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Manuel Bolieiro (page does not exist)">Jos\xc3\xa9 Manuel Bolieiro</a>. Although the Socialist Party dominates the regional politics, the Social Democratic Party is traditionally popular in city and <a href="/wiki/Town_council" title="Town council">town council</a> elections.\n</p><p>As part of Portugal, the Azores are in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. They are also in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union Customs Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax" title="Value-added tax">VAT</a> area<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> but levy a lower rate of VAT than applies on the mainland. The Azores, like Madeira and the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, are among <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">member state territories with special status</a>, as one of the designated "Outermost Regions".\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilha_das_Flores_P5300348_(35621052890).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Ilha_das_Flores_P5300348_%2835621052890%29.jpg/220px-Ilha_das_Flores_P5300348_%2835621052890%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Ilha_das_Flores_P5300348_%2835621052890%29.jpg/330px-Ilha_das_Flores_P5300348_%2835621052890%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Ilha_das_Flores_P5300348_%2835621052890%29.jpg/440px-Ilha_das_Flores_P5300348_%2835621052890%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2880" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilha_das_Flores_P5300348_(35621052890).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Country road on Flores Island</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation">Aviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Aviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lajes_field_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Lajes_field_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Lajes_field_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Lajes_field_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Lajes_field_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Lajes_field_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Lajes_field_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2207" data-file-height="1091" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lajes_field_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lajes_Air_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Lajes Air Base">Lajes Air Base</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Terceira_Island" title="Terceira Island">Terceira Island</a>, is a joint <a href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Air Force">U.S. Air Force</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Air_Force" title="Portuguese Air Force">Portuguese Air Force</a> military base.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aviation_in_the_Azores" title="Aviation in the Azores">Aviation in the Azores</a></div>\n<p>Each of the nine islands has an airport,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> although the majority are airfields rather than airports. The commercial terminals in Ponta Delgada, Horta, Vila do Porto and Santa Cruz das Flores are operated by <a href="/wiki/ANA_%E2%80%93_Aeroportos_de_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="ANA \xe2\x80\x93 Aeroportos de Portugal">ANA \xe2\x80\x93 Aeroportos de Portugal</a>, a public entity that oversees the operations of airports across Portugal. The remaining, except for <a href="/wiki/Lajes_Field" title="Lajes Field">Lajes Field</a>, are operated by the Regional Government. Lajes is a military airbase, as well as a commercial airport, and is operated by the Portuguese Armed Forces in conjunction with the United States.\n</p><p>The airports are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Santa Maria: <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_Airport_(Azores)" title="Santa Maria Airport (Azores)">Santa Maria Airport (LPAZ)</a></li>\n<li>S\xc3\xa3o Miguel: <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Paulo_II_Airport" title="Jo\xc3\xa3o Paulo II Airport">Jo\xc3\xa3o Paulo II Airport (LPPD)</a></li>\n<li>Terceira: <a href="/wiki/Lajes_Airport" title="Lajes Airport">Lajes Airport (LPLA)</a></li>\n<li>S\xc3\xa3o Jorge: <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jorge_Airport" title="S\xc3\xa3o Jorge Airport">S\xc3\xa3o Jorge Airport (LPSJ)</a></li>\n<li>Pico: <a href="/wiki/Pico_Airport" title="Pico Airport">Pico Airport (LPPI)</a></li>\n<li>Faial: <a href="/wiki/Horta_Airport" title="Horta Airport">Horta Airport (LPHR)</a></li>\n<li>Graciosa: <a href="/wiki/Graciosa_Airport" title="Graciosa Airport">Graciosa Airport (LPGR)</a></li>\n<li>Flores: <a href="/wiki/Flores_Airport" title="Flores Airport">Flores Airport (LPFL)</a></li>\n<li>Corvo: <a href="/wiki/Corvo_Airport" title="Corvo Airport">Corvo Airport (LPCR)</a></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_transportation">Marine transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Marine transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Miseric%C3%B3rdia_church_from_the_dam_Angra_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Miseric%C3%B3rdia_church_from_the_dam_Angra_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Miseric%C3%B3rdia_church_from_the_dam_Angra_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Miseric%C3%B3rdia_church_from_the_dam_Angra_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Miseric%C3%B3rdia_church_from_the_dam_Angra_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Miseric%C3%B3rdia_church_from_the_dam_Angra_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Miseric%C3%B3rdia_church_from_the_dam_Angra_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3182" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Miseric%C3%B3rdia_church_from_the_dam_Angra_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marina of <a href="/wiki/Angra_do_Hero%C3%ADsmo" title="Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo">Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Azores has had a long history of marine transport to overcome distances and establish inter-community contacts and trade. Consequently, the shipbuilding industry developed in many islands, from small fishing boats to whaling sloops and larger passenger services.<sup id="cite_ref-ALine_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALine-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Passenger traffic to the main islands (S\xc3\xa3o Miguel, Santa Maria, Terceira and Faial) began in the 17th century, and between the 18th\xe2\x80\x9319th century, the <i>Pico Yacht</i> controlled the lucrative summer traffic season.<sup id="cite_ref-ALine_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALine-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After 1871, the Insulana Shipping Company was the only entity responsible for regular traffic between the islands (except Corvo), Madeira and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-ALine_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALine-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Finally, cargo and passenger transportation ceased in the 1970s, and the ships were sold or converted into tuna fishing boats. For the next 20 years, commercial maritime service between the islands ceased (except between Faial-Pico and Lajes das Flores-Vila do Corvo).<sup id="cite_ref-ALine_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALine-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marina_of_Horta_at_sunrise,_Faial_Island,_Azores,_Portgual_(PPL2-Enhanced)_julesvernex2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Marina_of_Horta_at_sunrise%2C_Faial_Island%2C_Azores%2C_Portgual_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_julesvernex2.jpg/220px-Marina_of_Horta_at_sunrise%2C_Faial_Island%2C_Azores%2C_Portgual_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_julesvernex2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Marina_of_Horta_at_sunrise%2C_Faial_Island%2C_Azores%2C_Portgual_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_julesvernex2.jpg/330px-Marina_of_Horta_at_sunrise%2C_Faial_Island%2C_Azores%2C_Portgual_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_julesvernex2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Marina_of_Horta_at_sunrise%2C_Faial_Island%2C_Azores%2C_Portgual_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_julesvernex2.jpg/440px-Marina_of_Horta_at_sunrise%2C_Faial_Island%2C_Azores%2C_Portgual_%28PPL2-Enhanced%29_julesvernex2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5618" data-file-height="3965" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marina_of_Horta_at_sunrise,_Faial_Island,_Azores,_Portgual_(PPL2-Enhanced)_julesvernex2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The port of Horta is famed worldwide as a trans-Atlantic stop for yachts and sailors.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Transma%C3%A7or" title="Transma\xc3\xa7or">Transma\xc3\xa7or</a> (Transportes Mar\xc3\xadtimos A\xc3\xa7orianos, Lda.) was founded in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-Transmacor_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Transmacor-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The shipping company operates four to six daily connections between Horta and Madalena throughout the year, using its small fleet of ships, in addition to inter-island connections between Faial, Pico, S\xc3\xa3o Jorge and Terceira during the summer months.<sup id="cite_ref-Transmacor_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Transmacor-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> New initiatives began in the late 1990s: the catamaran <i>Iapetos</i> began services, followed by <i>Lady of Mann</i> and <i>Golfinho Azul</i> (chartered by A\xc3\xa7orline).<sup id="cite_ref-ALine2_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALine2-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Jobs_Yacht_Venus_in_Portugal_(Faial_Island).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Steve_Jobs_Yacht_Venus_in_Portugal_%28Faial_Island%29.jpg/220px-Steve_Jobs_Yacht_Venus_in_Portugal_%28Faial_Island%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="89" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Steve_Jobs_Yacht_Venus_in_Portugal_%28Faial_Island%29.jpg/330px-Steve_Jobs_Yacht_Venus_in_Portugal_%28Faial_Island%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Steve_Jobs_Yacht_Venus_in_Portugal_%28Faial_Island%29.jpg/440px-Steve_Jobs_Yacht_Venus_in_Portugal_%28Faial_Island%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="388" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Jobs_Yacht_Venus_in_Portugal_(Faial_Island).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a>\'s yacht <i><a href="/wiki/Venus_(yacht)" title="Venus (yacht)">Venus</a></i> at <a href="/wiki/Horta,_Azores" title="Horta, Azores">Horta</a> Marina</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2005, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atl%C3%A2nticoline&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Atl\xc3\xa2nticoline (page does not exist)">Atl\xc3\xa2nticoline</a> was established, providing transport services.<sup id="cite_ref-ALine_63-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALine-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, Atlanticoline was involved in a controversial rejection of a 750-passenger, 150-vehicle ship ordered from the Estaleiros de Viana do Castelo (ENVC).<sup id="cite_ref-ENVC_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENVC-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Atlantida</i>, a 50&#160;million Euro cruiser (as part of a two-ship deal with the other named <i>Anticiclone</i>) was rejected in 2009 by Atlanticoline for the under-performance of the power-plant.<sup id="cite_ref-ENVC_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENVC-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Although it would only result in a five-minute delay between islands, the public company rejected the ship, and the contract was broken over the builder\'s inability to deliver the required ship on time.<sup id="cite_ref-ENVC_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENVC-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> While the ship was being shopped to other interested parties (<a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Ch\xc3\xa1vez">Hugo Ch\xc3\xa1vez</a> once considered purchasing the ferryboat in 2010), no interested buyers appeared, and ENVC decided to cede the <i>Atlantida</i> to Atl\xc3\xa2nticoline as part of the latter\'s open international competition to charter two ships in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-ENVC_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENVC-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2011, the Regional Government announced that it would purchase 60% of Transma\xc3\xa7or, equivalent to 500,000 Euro of the company\'s capital.<sup id="cite_ref-StakeTransmacor_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StakeTransmacor-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> With this transaction the autonomous government of the Azores ceded control, of which it once had 88% of the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-StakeTransmacor_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StakeTransmacor-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The signed memorandum of understanding concluded negotiations between the various parties involved, under which the liability of Transma\xc3\xa7or (worth a total of 8&#160;million Euro) was divided equally between the government and businessman <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_E._Almeida" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 E. Almeida">Jos\xc3\xa9 E. Almeida</a>, who is now the holder of a majority stake in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-StakeTransmacor_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StakeTransmacor-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, the Regional Government approved the consolidation of the three individual port authorities (Administra\xc3\xa7\xc3\xa3o dos Portos do Tri\xc3\xa2ngulo e Grupo Ocidental, Administra\xc3\xa7\xc3\xa3o dos Portos da Terceira e Graciosa and the Administra\xc3\xa7\xc3\xa3o dos Portos das Ilhas de S\xc3\xa3o Miguel e Santa Maria) and regional Portos dos A\xc3\xa7ores into one entity that resulted in a 2.2&#160;million Euro cost savings, in addition to a reduction from 11 to three administrators.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Church_of_Jesuite_Collegium_Ponta_Delgada_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Church_of_Jesuite_Collegium_Ponta_Delgada_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Church_of_Jesuite_Collegium_Ponta_Delgada_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Church_of_Jesuite_Collegium_Ponta_Delgada_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Church_of_Jesuite_Collegium_Ponta_Delgada_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Church_of_Jesuite_Collegium_Ponta_Delgada_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Church_of_Jesuite_Collegium_Ponta_Delgada_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2589" data-file-height="2367" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Church_of_Jesuite_Collegium_Ponta_Delgada_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Architecture#Azores_Islands" title="Portuguese Architecture">architecture of the Azores</a> is characterized by the contrast between black volcanic stone and white stucco.</div></div></div>\n<p>Religious festivals, patron saints and traditional holidays mark the Azorean calendar. The most important religious events are tied with the festivals associated with the <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_the_Holy_Spirit" title="Cult of the Holy Spirit">cult of the Holy Spirit</a>, commonly referred to as the festivals of the Holy Spirit (or <i>Esp\xc3\xadrito Santo</i>), rooted in millenarian dogma and held on all islands from May to September. These festivals are very important to the Azorean people, who are primarily Roman Catholic, and combine religious rituals with processions celebrating the benevolence and egalitarianism of neighbours. These events are centred around <i>treatros</i> or <i>imp\xc3\xa9rios</i>, small buildings that host the meals, adoration and charity of the participants, and used to store the artefacts associated with the events. On Terceira, for example, these imp\xc3\xa9rios have grown into ornate buildings painted and cared for by the local brotherhoods in their respective parishes. The events focus on the members of local parishes, not tourists, but all are welcome, as sharing is one of the main principles of the festivals. Some limited events focus on tourists, including a public event that the city government of Ponta Delgada on the island of S\xc3\xa3o Miguel holds, which attracts visitors and locals.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Imp%C3%A9rio_do_Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo_-_Quatro_Ribeiras.jpg/234px-Imp%C3%A9rio_do_Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo_-_Quatro_Ribeiras.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="5472" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption"><i><a href="/wiki/Cult_of_the_Holy_Spirit#Imp\xc3\xa9rios" title="Cult of the Holy Spirit">Imp\xc3\xa9rios</a></i> of the <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_the_Holy_Spirit" title="Cult of the Holy Spirit">Cult of the Holy Spirit</a> are found throughout the Azores.</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SMG_PDL_20090517_SaoJose_FestaSSCristo03.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/SMG_PDL_20090517_SaoJose_FestaSSCristo03.JPG/220px-SMG_PDL_20090517_SaoJose_FestaSSCristo03.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/SMG_PDL_20090517_SaoJose_FestaSSCristo03.JPG/330px-SMG_PDL_20090517_SaoJose_FestaSSCristo03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/SMG_PDL_20090517_SaoJose_FestaSSCristo03.JPG/440px-SMG_PDL_20090517_SaoJose_FestaSSCristo03.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SMG_PDL_20090517_SaoJose_FestaSSCristo03.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Procession of the <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_Senhor_Santo_Cristo_dos_Milagres" title="Cult of Senhor Santo Cristo dos Milagres">Cult of the Holy Lord Christ of the Miracles</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Festival of the <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_Senhor_Santo_Cristo_dos_Milagres" title="Cult of Senhor Santo Cristo dos Milagres">Lord Holy Christ of the Miracles</a> (<i>Senhor Santo Cristo dos Milagres</i>) in Ponta Delgada is the largest individual religious event in the Azores and takes place on <a href="/wiki/Rogation_days" title="Rogation days">Rogation Sunday</a>. Pilgrims from within the Portuguese diaspora normally travel to Ponta Delgada to participate in an afternoon procession behind the image of Christ along the flower-decorated streets of the city. Although the solemn procession is only held on one day, the events of the Festival of Senhor Santo Cristo occur over a period of a week and involve a ritual of moving the image between the main church and convent nightly, ultimately culminating in the procession, which is televised within the Azores and to the Portuguese diaspora.\n</p><p>The Sanjoaninas Festivities in <a href="/wiki/Angra_do_Hero%C3%ADsmo" title="Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo">Angra do Hero\xc3\xadsmo</a> on Terceira are held in June honoring <a href="/wiki/Anthony_of_Padua" title="Anthony of Padua">Saint Anthony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">Saint Peter</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">Saint John the Baptist</a>, in a large religious celebration. The festival of <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Lourdes" title="Our Lady of Lourdes">Our Lady of Lourdes</a> (<i>Nossa Senhora de Lourdes</i>), <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> of whalers, begins in Lajes on Pico Island on the last Sunday of August and runs through the week\xe2\x80\x94Whalers Week. It is marked by social and cultural events connected to the tradition of <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whale hunting</a>. The Wine <a href="/wiki/Harvest_festival" title="Harvest festival">Harvest Festival</a> (<i>Festa das Vindimas</i>), takes place during the first week of September and is a century-old custom of the people of Pico.\n</p><p>On Corvo, the people celebrate their patron saint Nossa Senhora dos Milagres (Our Lady of Miracles) on 15 August every year in addition to the festivals of the Divine Holy Spirit. The Festival da Mar\xc3\xa9 de Agosto (August Sea Festival), takes place every year beginning on 15 August in Praia Formosa on Santa Maria. Also, the Semana do Mar (Sea Week), dedicated almost exclusively to <a href="/wiki/Watersport" class="mw-redirect" title="Watersport">water sports</a>, takes place in August in the city of Horta, on Faial.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnaval</a> is celebrated in the Azores. Parades and pageants are the heart of the Carnaval festivities. There is lively music, colorful costumes, hand-made masks, and floats. The traditional bullfights in the bullring are ongoing as is the running of bulls in the streets.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Azores&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span
